  Thought 5/15 

 The core challenge for timeline is managing multiple phases with different targets and timings. I need to think about the data structure:

```typescript
interface TimelineState {
  startTime: number
  currentCycleIndex: number
  activePhases: Map<string, {
    animation: Animation | null
    startTime: number
    completed: boolean
  }>
}
```

Each RAF tick checks elapsed time against each phase's delay. When elapsed >= phase.delay and phase not started, we:
1. Get the target element(s)
2. Call webAnimationPlugin or create Animation directly
3. Call phase.onStart callback
4. Mark phase as active

When elapsed >= (phase.delay + phase.duration), we call phase.onComplete and mark completed.

[ERROR] MCP server "sequential-thinking" Server stderr: 
  Thought 6/15 

 For loop management, when all phases complete (elapsed >= cycleDuration), I need to:
1. Emit onCycleComplete event
2. If loop enabled, wait loopDelay ms
3. Reset state: startTime = 0, activePhases.clear(), currentCycleIndex++
4. Emit onCycleStart event
5. Continue RAF loop

The tricky part is the loopDelay. I can't use setTimeout in the RAF loop directly because it breaks the timing. Instead, I'll track delayStartTime:
- When cycle completes, set delayStartTime = currentTime
- In RAF, check if (currentTime - delayStartTime >= loopDelay), then restart
- This keeps everything in RAF, no setTimeout needed

  Thought 7/15 

 Now thinking about phase animation creation. Each phase can have:
- animation.preset (like 'fadeIn')
- animation.keyframes (custom keyframes)
- animation.duration
- animation.easing

I need to reuse the existing animation creation logic. Looking at webAnimationPlugin and staggerPlugin, they both create Animation objects directly:

```typescript
const anim = el.animate(keyframes, {
  duration: effectiveDuration,
  easing: easing,
  fill: 'forwards'
})
```

For timeline, I'll do the same. Get keyframes from preset or use custom ones, then create Animation for each phase's target element(s).

[ERROR] MCP server "sequential-thinking" Server stderr: 
  Thought 8/15 

 For handling multiple targets per phase, I need to normalize the target:
- If single element: animate that element
- If array of elements: animate all in parallel
- If ref to element: resolve with toValue()
- If ref to array: resolve with toValue()

The phase can target different elements:
```typescript
{
  name: 'spark-travel',
  target: pathwayRefs,  // Ref<HTMLElement[]>
  delay: 0,
  duration: 1400
}
```

I'll need a helper function:
```typescript
function resolvePhaseTargets(target: MaybeRefOrGetter<HTMLElement | HTMLElement[]>): HTMLElement[] {
  const resolved = toValue(target)
  return Array.isArray(resolved) ? resolved : [resolved]
}
```

[ERROR] MCP server "sequential-thinking" Server stderr: 
  Thought 9/15 

 Thinking about integration with context.canAnimate and context.animationQuality. The timeline needs to respect environment settings:

- If canAnimate is false, skip all animations but still call callbacks
- If animationQuality is 'low', reduce durations by 70%
- If animationQuality is 'medium', reduce durations by 40%
- If animationQuality is 'none', skip animations entirely

This is already handled in staggerPlugin, I'll follow the same pattern:

```typescript
const effectiveDuration = phaseDuration * (
  context.animationQuality.value === 'low' ? 0.3 :
  context.animationQuality.value === 'medium' ? 0.6 : 1
)
```
